## Strategy in brief
EMA5/8/13 + RSI + ADX scalper on 5m, BTC-macro-gated. Entry passes a BTC/pair filter stack → sized by liquidity caps × multiplier/pattern-cell rules → exited by a tiered ladder.

### Exit stack (current)
- **FAST_EXIT OFF** (both L1 +0.20%/2min and L2 disabled).
- **ATR-LOW Fixed TP (LONG) — DISABLED 2026-06-09** (`atr_low_fixed_tp_long_enabled=false`). Paired with "Keep Only Unmatched Longs" (below): the fix-TP caps the pop-and-fade (matched) cohort, but the unmatched longs we now keep are RUNNERS (54% peak ≥0.40) — capping them at +0.25 strangled the edge. OFF so unmatched longs trail. **Coupling: re-enable the fix-TP if `long_unmatched_only` is ever turned OFF (matched longs need the cap).**
- **🧬 KEEP ONLY UNMATCHED LONGS — SHIPPED 2026-06-09 (in-sample, forward-test)** (`long_unmatched_only=true`). Blocks any LONG matching ANY C or W pattern (counter `LONG_UNMATCHED_ONLY`); keep only truly-unmatched longs. **Evidence (10-pool, current-stack: fix-TP + EMA13-off + wide-SL + multipliers):** the LONG pattern library uniformly selects for LOSERS — EVERY C/W pattern net-negative (W6 −$574, W2 −$480, C7 −$261, C6 −$297 demux; multiplier *amplifies* the matched losses); truly-unmatched longs = N=39, **85% WR, +$471 demux / +$679 as-sized** (the UNMATCHED-LONG 2× sits correctly on them). Mechanism: matched-long patterns = countertrend/exhaustion signatures (C7 bounce, W6 top); no-pattern = clean momentum runner. **FORWARD-TEST READ GATE: does the unmatched-long cohort hold ≥70% WR AND net-positive demux on N≥20 fresh full-stack? SHORT side already mirror-optimal (truly-unmatched shorts blocked; matched shorts carry the edge).
- **Trailing**: arms at peak ≥ **0.45%** (tp_min), exits at peak − **0.25%** (pullback, ATR-floored ×0.5 + 0.1/level widen).

Fixes high-ATR L1 whipsaws where the ATR-widened pullback exceeds the peak (peak +0.45 − pullback 0.67 = −0.22 → exits red on a pair that recovers). Self-scopes to L1 (L2+ always clears). ## 📋 GO-LIVE TODO (future — not urgent in paper; build before/at live scale-up)
- **① Balance→leverage schedule (de-lever-as-you-grow risk knob; sibling of liquidity sizing) — 2026-06-26.** New config field `leverage_balance_schedule = "0:20, 10000:15, 25000:10, 100000:5"` (balance_usd : max_lev tiers; empty = OFF = current 20×). Engine: one clamp where leverage is set — `sched_cap = _lookup_schedule(schedule, current_equity)` then `leverage = min(confidence_lev, sched_cap)`; sits alongside the existing hard-cap clamp, composes with cell `lev_mult`, fully deterministic (steps down automatically as balance crosses thresholds, no manual call). Observability: header readout ("lev cap: 15× @ $12k", like the GROSS gauge). **⚠ The tier VALUES above are round GUESSES — the whole point is that they should be DATA-DRIVEN from the tail-stressed blended-pool Kelly (see below), not placeholders.** Genuinely INERT at $3.7k (tier 0:20 → min(20,20)=20× = no change), so safe to ship off/empty. RATIONALE: compounding punishes variance quadratically (g≈μ−σ²/2; leverage scales μ∝L but σ²∝L²) → a +EV strategy at too-high leverage has NEGATIVE compound growth; fat gap-tail + correlated-dump pulls growth-optimal leverage below 20×; as stakes get real, shift growth-max → ruin-aversion (fractional Kelly). Ties to scaling roadmap (ruin risk = binding constraint).
  - **📐 v3 OPERATING PLAN (2026-07-02, operator-ratified — SUPERSEDES the 07-01 11-tier G/L design AND the guess tiers): working-capital reserve = PRIMARY (✅ BUILT 2026-07-02), coarse 4-tier lev schedule = backstop.** Architecture: slippage/capacity = per-pair 0.1% cap + $500k ceiling (adaptive, the TRUE capacity governor — a global gross target was the wrong tool, operator-corrected); ruin = `reserve_mode="working_capital"` + `working_capital_target` (tradeable = min(available, target), reserve auto-grows, withdrawals pull FROM the reserve; engine at the safe-reserve calc, UI = Reserve Mode dropdown 3rd option, D11 full; **superseded same day by the AUTO SCHEDULE — operator: "all automatic, not me putting 40000 manually"**: `reserve_mode="schedule"` + `reserve_schedule="10000:8000, 25000:17500, 50000:27500, 100000:40000, 150000:50000, 250000:70000, 500000:100000"` — ✅ SHIPPED **ON** (engine walks the v3 table itself via the same tier-lookup as the lev schedule; below $10k → no reserve = full balance, so inert today; between milestones the reserve absorbs ALL growth; withdrawals pull from the reserve and it self-rebuilds automatically — no config action ever needed).   - **✅ RESOLVED 2026-06-29 — ATR-SPECIFIC vol-scaling is REFUTED; the de-lever lever is GLOBAL only (this schedule), NOT per-pair sizing. CLOSES the "high-ATR tail" thread — do NOT re-litigate.** Tested constant-$-risk sizing (size ∝ 1/effective-SL, so the ATR-widened −1.20 pairs shrink to 0.58× to match a −0.70 trade's $ risk) on the screened pool: **total $ +$3001 → +$2240 = −$761 (−25%)** for only −21% per-trade σ — and the rough geometric check shows the −25% mean hit DWARFS the σ²/2 benefit, so it lowers compound growth too. Why: high-ATR is **net-POSITIVE** ($ by band: 0.47-0.80 = +$1628, ≥0.80 = +$1249; ≥0.80 wins +$1960 vs loses −$711) → vol-scaling de-sizes the WINNERS more than the losers (PUMP/SUI +1.0-1.9% runners > the −1.20 losers). **The −1.20 high-ATR losses (SKYAI/MANTA/AGLD) are NOT a gap-through — they hit the engine's ATR-WIDENED −1.20 stop by design (`sl_atr_multiplier=1.5` capped at `sl_atr_widen_floor_pct=−1.20`), the RIGHT exit for the net-positive high-ATR runners.** They are the irreducible left-tail cost of a +EV cohort (same wall as flip-shorts / unmatched-long cell — winners & losers feature-inseparable). EVERY angle now refuted: entry-filter (high-ATR wins), exit (fast-exit −$195 post-filter), cell-cut (inseparable), ATR-sizing (−$761). **The ONLY lever is GLOBAL de-lever = pure risk-appetite (ruin-aversion), NOT an optimization** — it sacrifices ~25%+ return for lower drawdown; pull it only if balance gets thin / ruin becomes the binding constraint. At a healthy balance the −1.20 losses are variance to tolerate.
  - **PREREQ (data, do FIRST): tail-stressed blended-pool Kelly.** Build a BLENDED long+short pool (full trade set across the curated batches, NOT flip-shorts only) and run `maximize g(e)=E[ln(1+e·m_i)]` with losers' fills stressed to their in-trade/post-exit troughs (paper truncates the tail at the clean SL → biases Kelly HIGH). Output = growth-optimal exposure → de-lever tiers. **Note 2026-06-26:** ran it on the FLIP-SHORT-ONLY 5-batch pool (N=104) → e*=**0×** in all 3 tail scenarios because that sleeve's mean is NEGATIVE (−0.014%/trade realized, −0.636% gap-stressed, worst −10.17%) → Kelly won't lever a zero-edge coin flip AT ALL. That's a verdict on the SLEEVE (de-lever the flip-short sleeve toward observation), not the account. The account number needs the LONG sleeve blended in (longs are the edge: today's batch +$960/+0.58%/trade). Expected blended answer ≈ 8–14× (below current 20×).
  - **📐 CAPITAL-SCALING STRATEGY (operator-chosen 2026-06-30 — DESIGN registered, BUILD DEFERRED until forward-validated & balance approaches the first tier; no-op at $3k).** Goal = **$1M *banked* (withdrawn), NOT $1M in-account** → less ruin exposure. Three composed knobs, with the primary being the RESERVE (not the leverage curve):
>     1. **Reserve as the PRIMARY de-risk knob, reframed as "fixed working capital".** Today `reserve` is static (`reserve_percentage=20`; engine line ~2124 `tradeable = balance − reserve`). Build a `reserve_mode="working_capital"` + `working_capital_target` ($, 0=off): `tradeable = min(available − floor, target)`, so the reserve % **auto-grows** with balance to keep deployed capital ≈ constant. WHY this over the leverage curve: our real tail is **5 CORRELATED positions stopping together** — reserve caps *total deployed* regardless of correlation (the leverage curve only shrinks each of the 5, still deploys all). Property: **max correlated-cluster loss stays clamped at a fixed $** (≈ working_capital × SL% × lev) no matter how big the account gets → true ruin bound. e.g. $50k working cap → ~$7-10k max cluster loss whether the account is $60k or $500k.
>     2. **⇒ The balance→leverage schedule (① above) then goes FLAT, not descending.** `exposure ≈ (1−reserve%)×lev` — with reserve fixing working capital, a *descending* lev curve would DOUBLE de-risk (kills compounding). So with working-capital mode ON: leverage stays **constant** on the working capital (and the ① schedule must be re-keyed to working-capital or disabled, else it reads TOTAL balance and de-levers twice). Pick ONE primary: **reserve-primary + flat lev** (recommended, better for the correlated tail) OR the ① descending-lev curve with reserve 0 — not both aggressive.
>     3. **Periodic REAL withdrawals still required.** Reserve protects vs *trading* losses but stays ON the exchange (platform/hack risk) and doesn't *realize* the $1M. Operator's skim plan (withdraw $100k per +$150k gained) is the realize step — but **calibrate the early phase**: a FIXED $150k threshold makes cycle-1 from a small base require a huge % run (+1500% from $10k) with nothing banked = max ruin exposure exactly when most fragile. FIX: **(a) return the initial stake ASAP** (once ~2-3×, pull the original capital → zero personal-ruin risk from day 1); **(b) skim proportionally early** (% of each gain), switching to the fixed $100k/$150k cadence only once the account is ~$100k+ where $150k is a sane %.
>     - **CALIBRATION (do FIRST, with data): the working_capital size is set from the forward MAX-DRAWDOWN + the correlation of the 5 concurrent positions (N≥30 forward), NOT guessed.** Ties to the tail-stressed Kelly prereq (line ~77). Build only when balance nears the first tier.
>     4. **📏 CAPACITY CEILING is the second calibration input (operator-ratified 2026-07-01 — "de-lever vs fixed $50k volume" resolved: SEQUENCED, fixed cap is the ENDGAME).** The strategy has a market-dictated max size: the edge (+0.2-0.4%/trade net) scalps thin alts and is fragile to slippage, which grows with order size — somewhere ~$10-30k/position marginal slippage eats the marginal edge, and no capital fixes that. So: de-lever/ramp = the transition; **fixed working capital (≈ fixed max tradable volume) = the destination** — it aligns with the real constraint, makes drawdown-% shrink automatically as balance grows (ruin→0), and is one revisable number vs a schedule to mis-tune. **Do NOT pick the cap a priori ($50k is a placeholder): measure it from `exit_slippage_pct` telemetry as size scales (slippage-vs-notional curve; cap where marginal slippage eats ≥~30% of the per-trade edge).** The binding calibration wins: min(risk-based cap from DD+correlation [pt 3], capacity cap from slippage). Linear in-account growth at the ceiling is FINE — wealth realizes via the withdrawal plan (pt 3), not in-account compounding. Want more than the ceiling? → a SECOND strategy (the parked BTC 4h Donchian module), never more size on this one.
- **② Server-side reduce-only stop-market backstop (closes the bot-outage gap-tail hole) — 2026-06-26.** Live SL is currently a SOFTWARE/monitored stop (bot watches WS price → fires market order w/ 3× bounded retry); NO resting exchange-side stop → a bot/WS outage or violent gap has no server-side safety net (the `protective_sl_order_id` column is vestigial/unwired). FIX: place a reduce-only STOP_MARKET on Binance at open so the exchange closes near the level even if the bot dies. **⚠ HISTORY: attempted before and REMOVED — it generated Binance errors on close trades** (likely reduce-only/qty/precision conflict with the bot's own market close racing the resting stop). So a re-attempt MUST solve the dual-close race (e.g. cancel the resting stop in the close path before the bot's own market close, or make the resting stop the SOLE close mechanism for SL exits). Not a paper concern (paper fills the SL clean at trigger, ~0 slippage); strictly a live-hardening item. The everyday live fill is ~SL+slippage (≈−1 to −1.5%), NOT the −4.77% worst-case trough; the resting stop closes the rare violent-gap/outage tail.

Track-only — quantify how often a short-cluster maps to a single BTC bounce before designing the cap.

If both → 70-80 is the clean 1.5×→2× cell.** **🔭 UPDATE 2026-07-02 — bear≥80 now a BLOCK candidate with its own pre-committed gate (3rd consistent window; operator-registered).** The 07-01/02 batch's Winners-vs-Losers cross-check killed every other flashy flip axis by baseline inversion (ADXΔ, RngPos, pair-gap, BTC-1h-slope, pair-vol$ ALL invert — the 1h-slope theory is refuted: baseline 1h>+0.10 flips are 88.9%WR, the BEST cohort; thin-pair theory refuted the same way) — **breadth was the ONLY survivor.** Combined bear≥80 record: **N=11, 5W/6L, 45.5%WR, −0.02% avg ≈ breakeven** — holds the sleeve's 4 worst losers (PUMP −1.24 / AGLD −1.21 / **ZBT −1.19** / WIF −1.16, + TIA −0.72; both fresh 07-01 zone entries LOST as the exhaustion thesis predicts) but ALSO the 2 biggest winners (ORDI +2.80, H +1.28). Confirm on clean single-config data. ─── orig theory + validation: THEORY (operator): high ATR = fast-resolving trades (hit the fixed ±% stops quickly, while the entry thesis still holds); low ATR = slow trades where BTC conditions drift from entry → random outcome. - **🔭 WATCHLIST (2026-06-17) — generalize the BE-ratchet to the NORMAL realtime trailing (active, decoupled breakeven floor).** Root cause of VELVET-type round-trips (armed peak +0.76 → −1.20 SL): the realtime trailing pullback trigger is ATR-FLOORED (`_effective_pullback = max(base, entry_atr × trailing_atr_multiplier=0.5)`), so on a high-ATR pair (VELVET ATR 1.59%) the give-back needed to ARM the trail is huge → it never crosses while in profit (`trailing_first_pullback_pnl_pct = −1.094` = first crossing was already at −1.09%) → the ATR-widened hard SL is the only exit. **`trailing_min_profit_to_fire`=0.1 does NOT cover this** — verified at [trading_engine.py:9127](services/trading_engine.py:9127) it's a SUPPRESSOR (cancels an already-triggered trailing close below 0.1, flips-only), the OPPOSITE of a floor — it removes exits below 0.1, never creates one, and it's COUPLED to the ATR-pullback trigger that didn't fire in time (on VELVET it even suppressed the −1.09 close → SL took it to −1.20). **PROPOSAL: an active, DECOUPLED BE-ratchet on the realtime path** — once `running_peak ≥ be_arm (0.45)`, force a close at `pnl ≤ be_lock (0.10)` regardless of the ATR-pullback (`reason TRAILING_BE_RATCHET`). Fixed P&L level → immune to the high-ATR scaling problem; direction-agnostic (covers flip-longs AND the short side as a backstop). VELVET: would exit ~+0.10 vs −1.20 (saves ~+1.30); shadow_tight (0.25 P&L give-back) +0.51 confirms a fixed floor works. Config: `trailing_be_ratchet_enabled` + `trailing_be_arm_pct=0.45` + `trailing_be_lock_pct=0.10`. **SCOPE decision pending: flips-only (lower blast radius, where the gap is seen) vs all trailing trades.** Caveat: caps a dip-then-rerun at the lock (bounded — banks a small win; lower the lock for more room). Note: this is the GENERAL version of the SHORT runner BE-ratchet already shipped (which is ATR-floor-specific + short-only).

- **🔀⚠️ FLIP CHAIN-POSITION BUG — WATCHLIST (identified 2026-06-15, NOT fixed; decision deferred to data).**
  **CORRECT DESIGN (the intent):** the flip should fade ONLY entries that *passed every filter and would have actually traded* but for the fan dead-zone — i.e. genuine "would-have-opened" longs (fan 0.85-3.00 / 5.0-99) and shorts (fan 1.00-1.90). For that, `FAN_RATIO_GATE` must be the **LAST** gate in the chain, so a fan-blocked entry is guaranteed to have cleared all other filters.
  **ACTUAL DESIGN (what's coded):** `FAN_RATIO_GATE` fires at **gate #8 of ~27** in `scan_and_trade` (line ~6771), and the flip opens *right there* — BEFORE ~19 downstream gates (`BTC_TREND_FILTER`, `BTC_SLOPE_*`, `BTC_1H_*`, `BTC_ACCEL_CHASE_LONG`, `PAIR_TREND_FILTER`, `VOL_GATE`, `BREADTH_GATE`, PAIR_ATR…). So flips fade a **contaminated SUPERSET**: entries that passed only the first 8 filters, NOT all of them. A fan-blocked long that would have failed a downstream gate (e.g. NEAR — a counter-trend bullish stack in a HEALTHY_BEAR that `BTC_TREND_FILTER`/`PAIR_TREND_FILTER` would likely have killed) still triggers a flip today. (Does NOT change which entries *trade* — fan-band entries are always blocked either way — only which ones *flip*; the phantom seeds at the same wrong point, so its +0.13% edge is on the superset too.)
  **COUNTERINTUITIVE TWIST (why not fixed blindly):** the downstream gates block *counter-trend* entries, so the "junk" longs they'd block are exactly the ones whose fade (SHORT) is **macro-aligned** (short with a bear) — and those won this batch (NEAR +0.40% pk, FARTCOIN +0.63% pk, N=2 = noise). The passed-all-filters longs are in *supportive* regimes → their fades are counter-trend-into-the-trend (the cohort steamrolled in STRONG_BULL). So fixing blindly might drop the WINNERS and keep the losers.
  **DECISION GATE (resolve with data, target N≥30 clean flips): deeply evaluate flip WINNERS vs LOSERS — primarily by REGIME ALIGNMENT (macro-aligned fade vs counter-trend fade, using captured `entry_macro_trend`/`entry_btc_regime`) and the Entry-Conditions-by-Outcome separators.** ① If a CLEAR loser-filter emerges (e.g. counter-trend fades lose, aligned win) → **KEEP the current mid-chain design and ADD that filter** to remove the losers (a regime-gate, NOT a chain move). ② If NO clean separator emerges → **revert to the CORRECT design: move `FAN_RATIO_GATE` + the flip trigger + the phantom seed to the END of the filter chain** (after `BREADTH_GATE`, before `open_position`), so flips only fire on genuine passed-all-filters entries — and re-validate the edge on the clean cohort. Until resolved: keep mid-chain (more volume = faster N for the split); cost is low (flip on 1× probation, net-negative regardless).
- **🔀🧪 REGIME-ALIGNMENT FINDING + FAN_CONTROL / FAN-RATIO-CURVE EXPERIMENT — shipped 2026-06-15 (phantom/observation-only, forward-only).** **THE FINDING (mechanism-backed, from the 2-batch flip split):** flip winners vs losers separate cleanly on **macro regime alignment, NOT the FAN signal.** A fade that aligns with the BTC EMA20 slope wins (aligned: ~88% WR / +$126 in-sample); a counter-trend fade loses (short into a RISING BTC: ~50% WR / −$120). Smoking gun = FARTCOIN: same pair, won its fade in a bear window, lost the SAME fade twice in a bull window. **Open question this experiment answers:** is the fan dead-zone (0.85-3.00/5.0-99 long, 1.00-1.90 short) actually *doing* anything, or is it incidental to regime alignment? **Two probes added:** ① **FAN_CONTROL phantom** — a virtual fade seeded when an entry's fan ratio is OUTSIDE the dead-zone (i.e. the entry PASSES the fan filter); it's the A/B control for FAN_RATIO_GATE — if FAN_CONTROL fades pay the SAME as FAN_RATIO_GATE fades (once regime-matched), the fan band earns nothing and the real signal is pure regime. Seeded in the fan gate's `for-else` branch (loop completes with no band match → fan outside dead-zone), fail-silent, never affects live. ② **FAN-RATIO CURVE** — a new `🔀 Phantom Flip` sub-table (`#phantom-fan-curve-body`, both text exports) that pools FAN_RATIO_GATE + FAN_CONTROL phantoms and buckets by fan ratio (0-0.85 / 0.85-1.0 / 1.0-1.35 / 1.35-1.65 / 1.65-2.0 / 2.0-3.0 / 3.0-5.0 / 5.0-99) × regime alignment (all / aligned / counter), flagging which buckets are in the dead-zone (DZ). Goal: find WHERE the aligned edge peaks across fan ratio → **define the best fan range for fades** (refines or replaces the dead-zone for the flip sleeve). **READ at N≥30 pooled fades/bucket: if the aligned edge is flat across ALL fan buckets (DZ and non-DZ alike) → the fan band is incidental; design the live flip sleeve as a pure REGIME-ALIGNMENT gate (fade only when macro-aligned, any fan). If the aligned edge concentrates in specific fan buckets → tighten the flip's fan range to those. Either way the live regime-alignment gate (deferred above) gets its fan window from this curve.** Friction wall still applies: phantom is frictionless, live pays ~0.27%/trade → +0.30% promotion bar on any bucket before it ships live.

## Metrics tracked
**Avg P&L %** (leverage-invariant — the comparison metric) · Daily Compound Return · per-cell verdict (Multiplier / Pattern-Cell Ship tables) · Filter Blocks counters · Gross gauge (% + $ tooltip) · entry/exit slippage · Pattern C/W trackers (observation-only).

## Known risks
- **Gross 30× tail**: a −3.3% correlated gap ≈ −100% equity (per-position SLs are primary protection; gross cap is flash-crash insurance).
- **Multiplier amplification on fat-tail losers**: C6/C1/W2 cohorts are 62-74% WR *winners* net-dragged by a few 3×-amplified losers → fix is surgical sizing on the specific losers, NOT blocking the cohort ("high-WR-but-net-losing" trap).
- **LONG book structurally weak** (negative in most cross-batch dimensions); LONG vol floor occasionally clips high-ATR runners.

## Do not change for now
- **BE stays OFF** (proven not to help; runner-trail + trailing is the current exit thesis (FAST_EXIT OFF too)).
- **SHORT volume rescue stays $0** (mirroring LONG $50M would un-block dead-tape SHORTs like SEI).
- **Don't add more entry filters reflexively** — 15+ already, diminishing returns. Exit-side + sizing is the active lever.

## Next ~1-week forward-test focus
1. **Liquidity-sizing live validation** — the Go-Live Watch signals (Gross gauge, GROSS_CAP_SKIP, ① slippage, REDEPLOY_OPEN=0).
2. **Global Vol filter** firing correctly + not clipping runners (VOL_GATE counters).
3. **ADX Δ filter** + the recent BTC RSI/ADX cross-filter openings holding.
4. Combined **Avg P&L %** vs the recent −$1,941/207-trade baseline; SHORT-side drag (dead-tape, C1/W2 amplified losers).
5. **Reset partition:** after the user's reset, analyze only `opened_at ≥ reset timestamp` (don't pool pre-reset trades).
